The GT expression with constants substituted is:

$$GT = 4.256 \cdot \epsilon^3 - 0.390(T - 308.86) + 8.638 \cdot \epsilon^3 (T - 308.86)$$

Let me expand this:

$$GT = 4.256\epsilon^3 - 0.390T + 0.390 \times 308.86 + 8.638\epsilon^3 T - 8.638 \times 308.86 \cdot \epsilon^3$$

$$GT = 4.256\epsilon^3 - 0.390T + 120.52 + 8.638\epsilon^3 T - 2667.5\epsilon^3$$

$$GT = 8.638 T\epsilon^3 - 0.390T + (4.256 - 2667.5)\epsilon^3 + 120.52$$

$$GT = 8.638 T\epsilon^3 - 0.390T - 2663.2\epsilon^3 + 120.52$$

So the GT is a function with terms: $T\epsilon^3$, $T$, $\epsilon^3$, and a constant.

The basis functions needed are: **T·ε³, T, ε³, constant (1)**.

## Checking Candidates

I need to find candidates that can produce exactly these four basis function terms: $T\epsilon^3$, $T$, $\epsilon^3$, and a constant.

Let me first expand $T \cdot c_0(c_1 + \epsilon)^3$, which appears in many candidates:

$$T \cdot c_0(c_1 + \epsilon)^3 = T \cdot c_0(c_1^3 + 3c_1^2\epsilon + 3c_1\epsilon^2 + \epsilon^3)$$

This gives terms: $T$, $T\epsilon$, $T\epsilon^2$, $T\epsilon^3$.

The GT has $T\epsilon^3$ and $T$ but **no** $T\epsilon$ or $T\epsilon^2$ terms. So we need $c_1 = 0$ to eliminate those. With $c_1 = 0$:

$$T \cdot c_0 \cdot \epsilon^3$$

This gives only $T\epsilon^3$. Good. Now we need additional terms to provide $T$, $\epsilon^3$, and a constant.

### Candidates with $T \cdot c_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + T \cdot c_2 + ... + \text{constant}$

**Candidate 5**: $T c_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + Tc_2 + Tc_3\epsilon + c_4\epsilon^2 + c_5\epsilon + c_6$

Set $c_1=0$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + Tc_2 + Tc_3\epsilon + c_4\epsilon^2 + c_5\epsilon + c_6$

We need $Tc_3\epsilon = 0$ → $c_3 = 0$, $c_4\epsilon^2 = 0$ → $c_4 = 0$, $c_5\epsilon = 0$ → $c_5 = 0$.

But then we have $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + Tc_2 + c_6$. This gives $T\epsilon^3$, $T$, constant — but **no ε³ term**. Missing basis function. ❌

**Candidate 26**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + Tc_2 + Tc_3\epsilon + c_4\epsilon^2 + c_5\epsilon$

Same issue — no $\epsilon^3$ or constant term available. ❌

**Candidate 31**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + Tc_2 + c_3\epsilon^2 + c_4\epsilon$

No $\epsilon^3$ or constant. ❌

**Candidate 35**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + Tc_2 + c_3 + c_4\epsilon^2 + c_5\epsilon$

Set $c_1=0$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + Tc_2 + c_3 + c_4\epsilon^2 + c_5\epsilon$. Has $T\epsilon^3$, $T$, constant, but no $\epsilon^3$. Has unwanted $\epsilon^2, \epsilon$ (set to 0). Still no $\epsilon^3$. ❌

**Candidate 57**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + c_2\epsilon^2 + c_3\epsilon + c_4$

Set $c_1=0$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + c_2\epsilon^2 + c_3\epsilon + c_4$. Has $T\epsilon^3$, constant, but no $T$ or $\epsilon^3$. ❌

Now, what if we **don't** set $c_1=0$? Then we get $T$, $T\epsilon$, $T\epsilon^2$, $T\epsilon^3$ from the cubic. We'd need to cancel $T\epsilon$ and $T\epsilon^2$ using other terms.

**Candidate 5**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + Tc_2 + Tc_3\epsilon + c_4\epsilon^2 + c_5\epsilon + c_6$

Expanding: $c_0c_1^3 T + 3c_0c_1^2 T\epsilon + 3c_0c_1 T\epsilon^2 + c_0 T\epsilon^3 + c_2 T + c_3 T\epsilon + c_4\epsilon^2 + c_5\epsilon + c_6$

For $T\epsilon^2$: coefficient $3c_0c_1 = 0$ → $c_0=0$ or $c_1=0$. If $c_1=0$, back to before. If $c_0=0$, we lose $T\epsilon^3$. ❌

**Candidate 34**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + Tc_2 + c_3\epsilon + c_4\epsilon^2 + c_5\epsilon + c_6$

Same structure as Candidate 5 essentially (with $c_3$ playing role of $Tc_3\epsilon$ being split). Actually no, this has no $T\epsilon$ term to cancel $3c_0c_1^2 T\epsilon$. Same issue. ❌

Let me look for candidates that have both $\epsilon^3$ and $T$ terms alongside $T\epsilon^3$.

**Candidate 1**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + c_2\epsilon^{c_3} + c_4\epsilon^2 + c_5\epsilon + c_6$

Set $c_1=0$, $c_3=3$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + c_2\epsilon^3 + c_4\epsilon^2 + c_5\epsilon + c_6$. Has $T\epsilon^3$, $\epsilon^3$, constant, but no $T$ term. ❌

**Candidate 24**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + Tc_2\epsilon + c_3\epsilon^3 + c_4\epsilon + c_5\epsilon^2 + c_6\epsilon + c_7$

Set $c_1=0$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + Tc_2\epsilon + c_3\epsilon^3 + (c_4+c_6)\epsilon + c_5\epsilon^2 + c_7$

Has $T\epsilon^3$, $\epsilon^3$, constant. But has $T\epsilon$ instead of $T$. Can't convert $T\epsilon$ to $T$. ❌

**Candidate 64**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + Tc_2\epsilon + c_3\epsilon + c_4\epsilon^3 + c_5\epsilon^2 + c_6\epsilon$

Set $c_1=0$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + Tc_2\epsilon + c_4\epsilon^3 + c_5\epsilon^2 + (c_3+c_6)\epsilon$. No $T$ or constant. ❌

**Candidate 55**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + Tc_2\epsilon + Tc_3 + c_4 + c_5\epsilon + c_6\epsilon + c_7\epsilon$

Set $c_1=0$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + Tc_2\epsilon + Tc_3 + c_4 + (c_5+c_6+c_7)\epsilon$

Has $T\epsilon^3$, $T$, constant. But has $T\epsilon$ (unwanted) and $\epsilon$ (unwanted, but can set to 0). Need $c_2=0$ to kill $T\epsilon$. Then: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + Tc_3 + c_4 + (c_5+c_6+c_7)\epsilon$. Set $c_5+c_6+c_7=0$. Result: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + Tc_3 + c_4$. Missing $\epsilon^3$. ❌

**Candidate 6**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + Tc_2\epsilon + Tc_3 + c_4 + c_5\epsilon + c_6\epsilon^2 + c_7\epsilon$

Set $c_1=0$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + Tc_2\epsilon + Tc_3 + c_4 + (c_5+c_7)\epsilon + c_6\epsilon^2$

Set $c_2=0, c_6=0, c_5+c_7=0$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + Tc_3 + c_4$. Missing $\epsilon^3$. ❌

Now let me look at candidates with $(T+c)^2$ terms, which expand to $T^2 + 2cT + c^2$ terms.

**Candidate 25**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + c_2\epsilon^3 + c_3\epsilon^2 + c_4 + c_5\epsilon(T+c_6)^2$

The $(T+c_6)^2$ term gives $T^2\epsilon$ which is not in GT. Unless $c_5=0$, but then we lose the $T$ dependence needed. ❌

**Candidate 28**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + c_2\epsilon^2 + c_3\epsilon + c_4(T+c_5)^2$

$c_4(T+c_5)^2 = c_4T^2 + 2c_4c_5T + c_4c_5^2$. Has $T^2$ which GT doesn't have. Need $c_4=0$, losing $T$ term. ❌

**Candidate 67**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + c_2\epsilon^3 + c_3\epsilon^2 + c_4\epsilon + c_5(T+c_6)^2$

Same issue — $T^2$ term. ❌

Now let me look at candidates with $T^{c_2}$ terms.

**Candidate 22**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + T^{c_2}c_3 + c_4\epsilon^2 + c_5\epsilon$

Set $c_1=0, c_2=1$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + c_3T + c_4\epsilon^2 + c_5\epsilon$. Has $T\epsilon^3$, $T$, but no $\epsilon^3$ or constant. ❌

**Candidate 32**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + T^{c_2}c_3 + c_4\epsilon^2 + c_5\epsilon$

Same as 22. ❌

**Candidate 3**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + T^{c_2}c_3 + c_4\epsilon^3 + c_5\epsilon^2 + c_6\epsilon + c_7\epsilon(T+c_8)^2$

Set $c_1=0$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + T^{c_2}c_3 + c_4\epsilon^3 + c_5\epsilon^2 + c_6\epsilon + c_7\epsilon(T+c_8)^2$

$c_7\epsilon(T+c_8)^2 = c_7\epsilon T^2 + 2c_7c_8\epsilon T + c_7c_8^2\epsilon$

Has $T^2\epsilon$ — not in GT. Need $c_7=0$. Then: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + T^{c_2}c_3 + c_4\epsilon^3 + c_5\epsilon^2 + c_6\epsilon$. Set $c_2=1$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + c_3T + c_4\epsilon^3 + c_5\epsilon^2 + c_6\epsilon$. Set $c_5=0, c_6=0$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + c_3T + c_4\epsilon^3$. Missing constant. 

But wait, set $c_2=0$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + c_3 + c_4\epsilon^3 + c_5\epsilon^2 + c_6\epsilon$. Has constant and $\epsilon^3$ but no $T$. ❌

Hmm. What about keeping $c_1 \neq 0$ and using other terms to cancel?

Let me reconsider. With $c_1 \neq 0$:

$Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 = c_0c_1^3 T + 3c_0c_1^2 T\epsilon + 3c_0c_1 T\epsilon^2 + c_0 T\epsilon^3$

GT needs: $a \cdot T\epsilon^3 + b \cdot T + c \cdot \epsilon^3 + d$

So from the cubic, we get $T\epsilon^3$ (good) and $T$ (from $c_0c_1^3 T$, good), but also unwanted $T\epsilon$ and $T\epsilon^2$. We need other terms to cancel these.

**Candidate 8**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + Tc_2 + Tc_3\epsilon + Tc_4\epsilon + c_5\epsilon + c_6\epsilon^2 + c_7\epsilon + c_8$

Expanding: $c_0c_1^3 T + 3c_0c_1^2 T\epsilon + 3c_0c_1 T\epsilon^2 + c_0 T\epsilon^3 + c_2T + (c_3+c_4)T\epsilon + (c_5+c_7)\epsilon + c_6\epsilon^2 + c_8$

$T\epsilon^2$ coefficient: $3c_0c_1 = 0$ → $c_1=0$ or $c_0=0$. Same issue. ❌

The problem is that no candidate has a $T\epsilon^2$ term to cancel $3c_0c_1 T\epsilon^2$.

**Candidate 65**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + Tc_2 + Tc_3\epsilon + c_4\epsilon^3 + c_5\epsilon^2 + c_6\epsilon + c_7\epsilon(T+c_8)^2$

$c_7\epsilon(T+c_8)^2 = c_7\epsilon T^2 + 2c_7c_8\epsilon T + c_7c_8^2\epsilon$

Has $T^2\epsilon$. Need $c_7=0$. Then same as Candidate 5 + $c_4\epsilon^3$. Set $c_1=0$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + Tc_2 + Tc_3\epsilon + c_4\epsilon^3 + c_5\epsilon^2 + c_6\epsilon$. Set $c_3=0, c_5=0, c_6=0$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + Tc_2 + c_4\epsilon^3$. Missing constant. ❌

Hmm, but wait — what about $c_1 \neq 0$ and using $c_7\epsilon(T+c_8)^2$ to provide $T\epsilon^2$?

$c_7\epsilon(T+c_8)^2 = c_7\epsilon T^2 + 2c_7c_8\epsilon T + c_7c_8^2\epsilon$

This has $T^2\epsilon$ which GT doesn't have. ❌

**Candidate 2**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^{c_2} + c_3\epsilon^3 + c_4\epsilon^2 + c_5\epsilon + c_6$

Set $c_2=3, c_1=0$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + c_3\epsilon^3 + c_4\epsilon^2 + c_5\epsilon + c_6$

Has $T\epsilon^3$, $\epsilon^3$, constant. But no $T$ term. ❌

What if $c_2 \neq 3$? Then we don't get $T\epsilon^3$. ❌

**Candidate 58**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^{c_2} + c_3\epsilon^2 + c_4\epsilon + c_5$

Same issue. ❌

**Candidate 10**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + Tc_2(c_3+\epsilon)^{c_4} + c_5\epsilon^2 + c_6\epsilon + c_7$

Set $c_1=0$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + Tc_2(c_3+\epsilon)^{c_4} + c_5\epsilon^2 + c_6\epsilon + c_7$

Set $c_4=0$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + Tc_2 + c_5\epsilon^2 + c_6\epsilon + c_7$. Has $T\epsilon^3$, $T$, constant. Missing $\epsilon^3$. ❌

Set $c_4=3, c_3=0$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + Tc_2\epsilon^3 + c_5\epsilon^2 + c_6\epsilon + c_7$. Two $T\epsilon^3$ terms combine. No $T$ or $\epsilon^3$ separately. ❌

**Candidate 27**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + Tc_2(c_3+\epsilon)^{c_4} + c_5\epsilon^2 + c_6\epsilon$

Similar to 10 but without constant. ❌

**Candidate 9**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + Tc_2\epsilon + Tc_3(c_4+\epsilon)^{c_5} + c_6\epsilon + c_7\epsilon^2 + c_8\epsilon + c_9$

Set $c_1=0$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + Tc_2\epsilon + Tc_3(c_4+\epsilon)^{c_5} + (c_6+c_8)\epsilon + c_7\epsilon^2 + c_9$

Set $c_5=0$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + Tc_2\epsilon + Tc_3 + (c_6+c_8)\epsilon + c_7\epsilon^2 + c_9$

Set $c_2=0, c_7=0, c_6+c_8=0$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + Tc_3 + c_9$. Missing $\epsilon^3$. ❌

**Candidate 53**: Same structure as 9 essentially. ❌

**Candidate 7**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + Tc_2\epsilon + T^{c_3}c_4 + c_5\epsilon + c_6\epsilon^2 + c_7\epsilon + c_8$

Set $c_1=0, c_3=1$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + Tc_2\epsilon + c_4T + (c_5+c_7)\epsilon + c_6\epsilon^2 + c_8$

Set $c_2=0, c_6=0, c_5+c_7=0$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + c_4T + c_8$. Missing $\epsilon^3$. ❌

**Candidate 21**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + Tc_2\epsilon + T^{c_3}c_4 + c_5\epsilon + c_6\epsilon + c_7\epsilon + c_8$

Same as 7 essentially. ❌

**Candidate 48**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + Tc_2\epsilon + c_3\exp(Tc_4) + c_5\epsilon + c_6\epsilon + c_7\epsilon + c_8$

Has exponential in T. GT doesn't. Need $c_3=0$. Then: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + Tc_2\epsilon + (c_5+c_6+c_7)\epsilon + c_8$ (with $c_1=0$). Missing $T$ and $\epsilon^3$. ❌

**Candidate 14**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + Tc_2\epsilon + c_3\epsilon^{c_4} + c_5\epsilon + c_6\epsilon + c_7\epsilon + c_8$

Set $c_1=0, c_4=3$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + Tc_2\epsilon + c_3\epsilon^3 + (c_5+c_6+c_7)\epsilon + c_8$

Has $T\epsilon^3$, $\epsilon^3$, constant. But has $T\epsilon$ (unwanted). Set $c_2=0$, $c_5+c_6+c_7=0$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + c_3\epsilon^3 + c_8$. Missing $T$. ❌

**Candidate 23**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + Tc_2\epsilon + c_3\epsilon^{c_4} + c_5\epsilon + c_6\epsilon^2 + c_7\epsilon + c_8$

Set $c_1=0, c_4=3$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + Tc_2\epsilon + c_3\epsilon^3 + (c_5+c_7)\epsilon + c_6\epsilon^2 + c_8$

Set $c_2=0, c_6=0, c_5+c_7=0$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + c_3\epsilon^3 + c_8$. Missing $T$. ❌

Now let me think differently. The GT has 4 basis functions: $T\epsilon^3$, $T$, $\epsilon^3$, $1$. I need a candidate that can produce all four.

Let me look at candidates that DON'T use the $(c_1+\epsilon)^3$ pattern.

**Candidate 68**: $c_0\epsilon^3 + c_1\epsilon^2 + c_2\epsilon^{c_3} + c_4\epsilon + c_5\exp(Tc_6) + c_7$

No $T\epsilon^3$ term possible. ❌

**Candidates 38, 39, 46, 47, 51, 62, 69, 70**: These have complex rational/exponential structures. Let me check if any can simplify to the GT form.

These involve $\exp(c_3\epsilon)$ and rational functions of $\epsilon$. GT is polynomial in $\epsilon$. These can't match unless the exponentials cancel, which would require very specific conditions. ❌

Now let me reconsider candidates with $\epsilon(T+c)^2$ terms more carefully.

$\epsilon(T+c)^2 = \epsilon T^2 + 2c\epsilon T + c^2\epsilon$

This has $T^2\epsilon$ which is not in GT. So these can't help unless coefficient is 0.

**Candidate 43**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + c_2\epsilon^3 + c_3\epsilon + c_4\epsilon(T+c_5)^2$

Set $c_1=0$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + c_2\epsilon^3 + c_3\epsilon + c_4\epsilon T^2 + 2c_4c_5\epsilon T + c_4c_5^2\epsilon$

Has $T^2\epsilon$. Need $c_4=0$. Then: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + c_2\epsilon^3 + c_3\epsilon$. Missing $T$ and constant. ❌

**Candidate 30**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + c_2\epsilon^3 + c_3 + c_4\epsilon + c_5\epsilon(T+c_6)^2$

Set $c_1=0, c_5=0$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + c_2\epsilon^3 + c_3 + c_4\epsilon$. Missing $T$. ❌

**Candidate 41**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + c_2\epsilon^3 + c_3\epsilon^2 + c_4\epsilon + c_5\epsilon(T+c_6)^2 + c_7\epsilon + c_8$

Same issue with $T^2\epsilon$. ❌

**Candidate 20**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + c_2\epsilon^2 + c_3\epsilon + c_4 + c_5\epsilon(T+c_6)^{c_7}$

Set $c_7=1$: $c_5\epsilon(T+c_6) = c_5\epsilon T + c_5c_6\epsilon$. 

Set $c_1=0$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + c_2\epsilon^2 + c_3\epsilon + c_4 + c_5\epsilon T + c_5c_6\epsilon$

Has $T\epsilon^3$, $T\epsilon$, constant, $\epsilon^2$, $\epsilon$. No $T$ or $\epsilon^3$. ❌

What if $c_7=0$? Then $c_5\epsilon \cdot 1 = c_5\epsilon$. No help. ❌

**Candidate 42**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + c_2\epsilon^{c_3} + c_4\epsilon^3 + c_5\epsilon^2 + c_6\epsilon + c_7\epsilon(T+c_8)^2$

$c_7\epsilon(T+c_8)^2$ has $T^2\epsilon$. Need $c_7=0$. Set $c_1=0, c_3=0$ (so $c_2\epsilon^0 = c_2$): $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + c_2 + c_4\epsilon^3 + c_5\epsilon^2 + c_6\epsilon$. Has $T\epsilon^3$, $\epsilon^3$, constant. Missing $T$. ❌

Hmm, what about $c_3$ being something else? If $c_7=0$, set $c_1=0$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + c_2\epsilon^{c_3} + c_4\epsilon^3 + c_5\epsilon^2 + c_6\epsilon$. No $T$ term available. ❌

**Candidate 66**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + Tc_2(c_3+\epsilon)^{c_4} + c_5\epsilon^3 + c_6\epsilon^2 + c_7\epsilon + c_8\epsilon(T+c_9)^2$

$c_8\epsilon(T+c_9)^2$ has $T^2\epsilon$. Need $c_8=0$.

Set $c_1=0$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + Tc_2(c_3+\epsilon)^{c_4} + c_5\epsilon^3 + c_6\epsilon^2 + c_7\epsilon$

Set $c_4=0$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + Tc_2 + c_5\epsilon^3 + c_6\epsilon^2 + c_7\epsilon$

Set $c_6=0, c_7=0$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + Tc_2 + c_5\epsilon^3$

This has $T\epsilon^3$, $T$, $\epsilon^3$! But missing constant. ❌

Hmm, so close! If only there were a constant term...

Wait, let me re-examine. Actually, $Tc_2(c_3+\epsilon)^{c_4}$ with $c_4=0$ gives $Tc_2 \cdot 1 = Tc_2$. But what if I don't set $c_4=0$?

If $c_3=0, c_4=3$: $Tc_2\epsilon^3$. Combined with $Tc_0\epsilon^3$, just gives $T\epsilon^3$. No $T$. ❌

What about non-integer $c_4$? That would introduce non-polynomial terms. ❌

**Candidate 40**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + Tc_2/(c_3\epsilon+c_4) + c_5\epsilon^2 + c_6\epsilon + c_7/(c_3\epsilon+c_4)$

This has rational terms in $\epsilon$. GT is polynomial. Need $c_2=0$ and $c_7=0$. Then: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + c_5\epsilon^2 + c_6\epsilon$ (with $c_1=0$). Missing $T$, $\epsilon^3$, constant. ❌

Let me look at candidates with $\exp(Tc)$ terms.

**Candidate 33**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + c_2\epsilon^2 + c_3\exp(Tc_4) + c_5\epsilon + c_6$

$\exp(Tc_4)$ is not polynomial in $T$. GT is polynomial. Need $c_3=0$. Then: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + c_2\epsilon^2 + c_5\epsilon + c_6$ (with $c_1=0$). Missing $T$ and $\epsilon^3$. ❌

**Candidate 49**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + c_2\epsilon^2 + c_3\exp(Tc_4) + c_5\epsilon$

Same. ❌

**Candidate 63**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^{c_2} + c_3\epsilon^3 + c_4\epsilon^2 + c_5\epsilon + c_6\exp(Tc_7) + c_8$

Need $c_6=0$. Set $c_2=3, c_1=0$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + c_3\epsilon^3 + c_4\epsilon^2 + c_5\epsilon + c_8$. Has $T\epsilon^3$, $\epsilon^3$, constant. Missing $T$. ❌

**Candidate 50**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + c_2\exp(c_3\epsilon) + c_4\epsilon^2 + c_5\epsilon$

$\exp(c_3\epsilon)$ is not polynomial. Need $c_2=0$. Then missing terms. ❌

**Candidate 29**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + c_2\epsilon^3 + c_3\exp(Tc_4) + c_5\epsilon^2 + c_6\epsilon + c_7\epsilon(T+c_8)^2$

Need $c_3=0$ and $c_7=0$. Set $c_1=0$: $Tc_0\epsilon^3 + c_2\epsilon^3 + c_5\epsilon^2 + c_6\epsilon$. Missing $T$ and constant. ❌

Let me look at candidates with $\log$ terms.

**Candidate 36**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + c_2\epsilon^2 + c_3\log(Tc_4+1) + c_5\epsilon + c_6$

$\log$ is not polynomial. Need $c_3=0$. Then missing terms. ❌

**Candidate 11**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + Tc_2\epsilon + c_3\log(Tc_4+1) + c_5\epsilon + c_6\epsilon^2 + c_7\epsilon + c_8$

Same issue. ❌

**Candidate 56**: Same. ❌

**Candidate 61**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + c_2\sin(Tc_3+c_4) + c_5\epsilon^2 + c_6\epsilon + c_7$

$\sin$ is not polynomial. Need $c_2=0$. ❌

**Candidate 12**: $Tc_0(c_1+\epsilon)^3 + Tc_2\epsilon + c_3\sin(Tc_4+c_5) + c_6\epsilon + c_7\epsilon^2 + c_8\epsilon + c_9$

Has T*epsilon³, epsilon³, constant. Missing T. **NO MATCH**

Actually, wait. Let me reconsider using c1≠0 more carefully. With c1≠0:

`T*c0*(c1+epsilon)³` = `T*c0*c1³ + 3T*c0*c1²*epsilon + 3T*c0*c1*epsilon² + T*c0*epsilon³`

This gives T (from T*c0*c1³), T*epsilon, T*epsilon², T*epsilon³.

I need to cancel T*epsilon and T*epsilon². If the candidate has additional terms with T*epsilon and T*epsilon², I can cancel them.

But most candidates don't have T*epsilon² terms. So I need 3*c0*c1=0, meaning c1=0.

Unless... the candidate has another `(c+epsilon)^3` term or similar.

**Candidate 9:** `T*c0*(c1+epsilon)**3 + T*c2*epsilon + T*c3*(c4+epsilon)**c5 + c6*epsilon + c7*epsilon**2 + c8*epsilon + c9`
If c5=3: Two cubic terms in T. Let me expand both:
`T*c0*(c1+epsilon)³ + T*c3*(c4+epsilon)³`
= T*[c0*(c1+epsilon)³ + c3*(c4+epsilon)³]

This is T times a cubic in epsilon. The cubic has terms: epsilon³, epsilon², epsilon, constant.

So: T*(c0+c3)*epsilon³ + T*(3c0*c1+3c3*c4)*epsilon² + T*(3c0*c1²+3c3*c4²)*epsilon + T*(c0*c1³+c3*c4³)

Plus: T*c2*epsilon + (c6+c8)*epsilon + c7*epsilon² + c9

Total T*epsilon² coefficient: 3c0*c1 + 3c3*c4 = 0 → c3*c4 = -c0*c1
Total T*epsilon coefficient: 3c0*c1² + 3c3*c4² + c2

For GT, T*epsilon coeff = 0: 3c0*c1² + 3c3*c4² + c2 = 0
T*epsilon² coeff = 0: 3(c0*c1 + c3*c4) = 0

These are satisfiable. Then:
- T*epsilon³ coeff: c0+c3
- T coeff: c0*c1³ + c3*c4³
- epsilon³: 0 (no epsilon³ term without T)
- Missing epsilon³! Only has epsilon² and epsilon standalone. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 10:** `T*c0*(c1+epsilon)**3 + T*c2*(c3+epsilon)**c4 + c5*epsilon**2 + c6*epsilon + c7`
If c4=3: Two T*cubic terms. Same as above analysis for T terms.
Standalone: c5*epsilon² + c6*epsilon + c7. No epsilon³. **NO MATCH**

If c4=0: `T*c2*1 = T*c2`. Then with c1=0: `T*c0*epsilon³ + T*c2 + c5*epsilon² + c6*epsilon + c7`
Has T*epsilon³, T, constant. Missing epsilon³. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 27:** `T*c0*(c1+epsilon)**3 + T*c2*(c3+epsilon)**c4 + c5*epsilon**2 + c6*epsilon`
Similar to 10 but no constant. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 53:** `T*c0*(c1+epsilon)**3 + T*c2*epsilon + T*c3*(c4+epsilon)**c5 + c6*epsilon + c7*epsilon + c8*epsilon + c9`
If c5=0: `T*c3*1 = T*c3`. With c1=0: `T*c0*epsilon³ + T*c2*epsilon + T*c3 + (c6+c7+c8)*epsilon + c9`
Set c2=0: `T*c0*epsilon³ + T*c3 + (c6+c7+c8)*epsilon + c9`
Has T*epsilon³, T, constant. Missing epsilon³. **NO MATCH**

Let me look at candidates with explicit epsilon**3 AND T terms:

**Candidate 65:** `T*c0*(c1+epsilon)**3 + T*c2 + T*c3*epsilon + c4*epsilon**3 + c5*epsilon**2 + c6*epsilon + c7*epsilon*(T+c8)**2`
With c1=0: `T*c0*epsilon³ + T*c2 + T*c3*epsilon + c4*epsilon³ + c5*epsilon² + c6*epsilon + c7*epsilon*(T+c8)²`
The (T+c8)² gives T²*epsilon. Set c7=0.
Result: `T*c0*epsilon³ + T*c2 + T*c3*epsilon + c4*epsilon³ + c5*epsilon² + c6*epsilon`
Set c3=0, c5=0, c6=0: `T*c0*epsilon³ + T*c2 + c4*epsilon³`
Has T*epsilon³, T, epsilon³. Missing constant. **NO MATCH**

Hmm, what about c7≠0? Then c7*epsilon*(T²+2c8*T+c8²) = c7*epsilon*T² + 2c7*c8*epsilon*T + c7*c8²*epsilon. The T²*epsilon can't be cancelled. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 71:** `T*c0*(c1+epsilon)**3 + T*c2 + c3 + c4*epsilon**3 + c5*epsilon**2 + c6*epsilon + c7*epsilon*(T+c8)**2`
With c1=0: `T*c0*epsilon³ + T*c2 + c3 + c4*epsilon³ + c5*epsilon² + c6*epsilon + c7*epsilon*(T+c8)²`
Set c7=0: `T*c0*epsilon³ + T*c2 + c3 + c4*epsilon³ + c5*epsilon² + c6*epsilon`
Set c5=0, c6=0: `T*c0*epsilon³ + T*c2 + c3 + c4*epsilon³`

This has: T*epsilon³ ✓, T ✓, constant ✓, epsilon³ ✓. And nothing else!

**This matches!** GT = a*T*epsilon³ + b*epsilon³ + c*T + d

Let me verify: c0 can give the T*epsilon³ coefficient, c2 gives the T coefficient, c3 gives the constant, c4 gives the epsilon³ coefficient. With c1=0, c5=0, c6=0, c7=0.

Candidate 71 verdict: **MATCH**

**Candidate 38:** Complex rational expression. Let me check if it simplifies.
All terms have `1/(c1+epsilon)` factor. Multiply through:
`[T*c0*epsilon + T*c2*epsilon*(c3+epsilon)³ + T*c4 + T*c5*(c3+epsilon)³ + c6 + (c7+c8)*epsilon] / (c1+epsilon)`

Numerator: T*[c0*epsilon + c2*epsilon*(c3+epsilon)³ + c4 + c5*(c3+epsilon)³] + c6 + (c7+c8)*epsilon

This is a rational function in epsilon (degree 4 numerator / degree 1 denominator). GT is polynomial. For this to be polynomial, (c1+epsilon) must divide the numerator. This is possible but constraining. The result would be a cubic in epsilon times T plus quadratic. Could potentially match but it's very constrained. Let me check if it can produce T*epsilon³ + epsilon³ + T + constant.

Actually, `T*c5*(c3+epsilon)³ + T*c2*epsilon*(c3+epsilon)³ = T*(c3+epsilon)³*(c5+c2*epsilon)`. This is degree 4 in epsilon times T. Divided by (c1+epsilon), if c1=c3, we could factor... This is getting complex. Let me set c2=0 to simplify:

Numerator: T*[c0*epsilon + c4 + c5*(c3+epsilon)³] + c6 + (c7+c8)*epsilon

= T*c5*epsilon³ + T*(3c5*c3)*epsilon² + T*(3c5*c3²+c0)*epsilon + T*(c5*c3³+c4) + c6 + (c7+c8)*epsilon

Dividing by (c1+epsilon): for this to be polynomial, (c1+epsilon) must divide the numerator. This requires the numerator to be zero at epsilon=-c1. This gives one constraint. The quotient would be degree 3 in epsilon (for T terms) plus constants. This could potentially work but requires very specific relationships. It's unlikely to simplify to exactly T*epsilon³ + epsilon³ + T + constant without additional epsilon³ terms. **NO MATCH** (too constrained, missing standalone epsilon³)

`T*c0*epsilon³ + T*c2 + c3 + c4*epsilon³`

= c0*T*epsilon³ + c4*epsilon³ + c2*T + c3

GT = 8.638*T*epsilon³ - 2663.88*epsilon³ - 0.39029*T + 120.546

So: c0 = 8.638, c4 = -2663.88, c2 = -0.39029, c3 = 120.546, c1=0, c5=0, c6=0, c7=0, c8=anything.
